  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_547e9b7a-f81b-4a36-a045-3f8166924868'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer12314361140218338251"><b>A captivating and utterly original fairy tale about a girl cursed to be poisonous to the touch, and who discovers what power might lie in such a curse...</b><br/><b></b><br/>There was and there was not, as all stories begin, a princess cursed to be poisonous to the touch. But for Soraya, who has lived her life hidden away, apart from her family, safe only in her gardens, it’s not just a story.</span>
  <span id="freeText12314361140218338251" style="display:none"><b>A captivating and utterly original fairy tale about a girl cursed to be poisonous to the touch, and who discovers what power might lie in such a curse...</b><br /><b></b><br />There was and there was not, as all stories begin, a princess cursed to be poisonous to the touch. But for Soraya, who has lived her life hidden away, apart from her family, safe only in her gardens, it’s not just a story.<br /><br />As the day of her twin brother’s wedding approaches, Soraya must decide if she’s willing to step outside of the shadows for the first time. Below in the dungeon is a demon who holds knowledge that she craves, the answer to her freedom. And above is a young man who isn’t afraid of her, whose eyes linger not with fear, but with an understanding of who she is beneath the poison.<br /><br />Soraya thought she knew her place in the world, but when her choices lead to consequences she never imagined, she begins to question who she is and who she is becoming...human or demon. Princess or monster.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12314361140218338251" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<div id="review_3177363821" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3177363821" />
    <a title="chai ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42130592-chai"><img alt="chai ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603167303p2/42130592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3177363821?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chai ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chai ♡" href="/user/show/42130592-chai">chai ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3177363821" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11747391692118446469">✧ <a href='https://bookswithchaima.wordpress.com/2020/06/23/review-girl-serpent-thorn-by-melissa-bashardoust/#more-3216' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <b>find this review & others on my blog</b>
</a> ✧<br/><br/>The story of the Shah’s twin sister came to the people of Atashar as most rumors do, as a drifting set of jokes and have-you-heards that combined and recombined themselves slowly into a single tale: a poisonous girl with the blood of a div moving in her veins, a burden to her family, living in the shadows, cursed and reviled.<br/><br/> <b>But unlike most rumors, this one is true.</b><br/><br/><br/> Soraya knows fear in the shape of her own face. She felt it in her poisonous blood, an</span>
  <span id="freeText11747391692118446469" style="display:none">✧ <a href="https://bookswithchaima.wordpress.com/2020/06/23/review-girl-serpent-thorn-by-melissa-bashardoust/#more-3216" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>find this review &amp; others on my blog</b>
</a> ✧<br /><br />The story of the Shah’s twin sister came to the people of Atashar as most rumors do, as a drifting set of jokes and have-you-heards that combined and recombined themselves slowly into a single tale: a poisonous girl with the blood of a div moving in her veins, a burden to her family, living in the shadows, cursed and reviled.<br /><br /> <b>But unlike most rumors, this one is true.</b><br /><br /><br /> Soraya knows fear in the shape of her own face. She felt it in her poisonous blood, an iron weight she had borne for so long. But it was a familiar feeling: the nagging sense that she was teetering on a knife’s edge, and all it would take was one push in the wrong direction and she would surrender to the deepest pull of the darkness that prowled inside her.<br /><br /> For years, Soraya has walked the edges of her curse, looking for a crack, but it held on. Until Azad, a handsome young soldier captures a female div named Parvaneh, and all the hope Soraya had shut out comes roaring back in. Parvaneh might be the only one who can show Soraya the gaps between the bars of her curse, but to escape her life, Soraya might have to tear a hole in her family’s.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Aren’t you made for death? </i>
</blockquote><br /><br /> The premise promises a story that bears the indentations of a dark and twisted fairytale with all the rich density of horror, a tale that gathers Persian mythology into an exhilarating antiheroic slant, a world where the truth of who is right or wrong is as cold and unreachable as the stars—and the potential is definitely there.<br /><br /> The novel is heavy on the foreshadowing: the story often feels like a clock winding tighter as the ending draws near, and the world—though only delicately sketched since the author does not explain or engage with every aspect of its nature—is sharpened with urgency. There’s a suggestion of a trapdoor waiting under every page, and the possibilities bristled in my thoughts.<br /><br /> Soraya is an interesting protagonist. She was shot through with that dark, smoky core of poison, and it sung in her. It bloomed power in her blood, and made her something more than human. It made her unstoppable. A kind of awful pleasure sliced through Soraya at the realization that she’s far more powerful than she’s ever given herself credit for, a question winding around her like a rope: “What would she allow herself to become?” The helpless girl, locked away and withering on the vine of life? The quiescent serpent, ignoring the coiled thing inside her, that gathering of something hard and unyielding? Or the girl made of thorns as long as spears and as sharp as needs, with a sting like fire?<br /><br /> When the tilted emptiness that has settled inside Soraya begins to fade, replaced by stubborn determination, I wanted—abruptly and with an absurd intensity—for her to kindle it, to shield and nurture that flame until it takes far more than a single breath to blow it out. And for a while, I thought the story would balloon in that direction. But the narrative often retreats into a flimsy plot populated with characters that could have been more substantially fleshed out, and culminating eventually into a big reveal that’s obvious from the book’s earliest pages—and one that isn’t all that gripping in the first place.<br /><br /> Ultimately, that’s my biggest quibble with the story—that it cries out for a more challenging, better developed execution of a really involved and interesting premise. Still that’s not enough to put a permanent dent in the novel’s spell. As the story powers forward, and Soraya is forced to brush with her moral code, the novel probes, painstakingly, at Soraya’s desire to be just, to somehow behave well despite the contradictory desires of the heart. The author also affectingly articulates the ways that humanizing and dehumanizing those we love can be flip sides of the same coin. Here, I wish the novel had dwelled longer on the sapphic romance that blossoms between Soraya and Parvaneh who, amid the swirling chaos, have looked at each other and found a possibility of something.<br /><br /> All quibbles aside, this was a solid read. I just wish I enjoyed it more.<br /><br /><blockquote>☆ <a href="https://ko-fi.com/givemeabrekk" rel="nofollow noopener">ko-fi</a> ★ <a href="https://bookswithchaima.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a> ☆ <a href="https://twitter.com/givemeabrekk" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a> ★ <a href="https://azqaban.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">tumblr</a> ☆</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="11747391692118446469" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3072180540" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3072180540" />
    <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik"><img alt="Nilufer Ozmekik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559807601p2/53701594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3072180540?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nilufer Ozmekik" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik">Nilufer Ozmekik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3072180540" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11374446691940016338">A poisonous girl threatens the people’s lives who dare to touch her (intentionally or accidentally) Poor Soraya suffers from loneliness, is exiled from her inner circle, living in the shadows because poison flows through her veins and she can kill somebody anytime. But a mysterious boy gets interested with her situation and he seems like he is not afraid of her.<br/><br/> You may think what a great pilot, the boy will break the curse, fight with the demons and ride to the sunset singing “take my horse to </span>
  <span id="freeText11374446691940016338" style="display:none">A poisonous girl threatens the people’s lives who dare to touch her (intentionally or accidentally) Poor Soraya suffers from loneliness, is exiled from her inner circle, living in the shadows because poison flows through her veins and she can kill somebody anytime. But a mysterious boy gets interested with her situation and he seems like he is not afraid of her.<br /><br /> You may think what a great pilot, the boy will break the curse, fight with the demons and ride to the sunset singing “take my horse to the Old Town Road, duct taping Billy Ray Cyrus’ mouth not to join him singing! Nope, when you reach half of the book, you just say “oh, I didn’t see it coming, it just moved to the different direction! Actually this book makes you feel like you read more than one books (I think a trilogy is hidden inside of this story and I wish the author told Soraya’s beautiful, emotional, awakening, self-discovery story in more than one book.)<br /> <br />So this fairy tale mixed with Persian culture and magical elements kind of story. A girl does not want to use her curse to gain power and threat people’s lives. She accepts her unfair faith and we catch glimpses from her early life and witness that she had a crush to a girl which is reciprocated. (Yes, we have a bisexual heroine on the board which is a different and unique touch) And yes, Soraya loves to see the roses’ growing because instead of killing or hurting any living thing, she wants to give them live and see them grow.<br /> <br /> Second part, we just realize, main love interest of this story is f/f relationship. But as I said from the beginning, this is not romantic fantasy about a girl who needs to love for breaking her curse and having her HEA! When we learn more about both of their skeletons they hid in their closets, we may see they are so flawless, pure, golden-hearted characters. So we have two realistically developed female characters’ uniquely developed story, are ready to atone their sins because they are not the villanelles. They are just humans who made mistakes and wrong choices in their pasts and now they want to correct them.<br /><br /> Overall this book is definitely not only a love story, it’s about a girl’s evolution, learning from her mistakes, choosing what she wants from her life, discovering her own strengths, sensibilities and forming her own path story . World building with Persian cultural elements and magical touch is also one of the best parts I truly enjoyed about the book.<br />I have to admit longevity of this book made me a little hesitated before I decided to start it. I still wish the story could have told in more than one book because the writing is intriguing, characters are easy to connect, pacing is balanced ( not too fast or slow).If you keen on reading some original, different approach with feminist vibes to the fairy tales, this book is definitely a great choice.<br /><br /> I gave 3.5 stars and of course the author’s hard efforts and lyrical, magical story-telling forced me to round it up to 4 stars.<br /><br />So much thanks to NetGalley and Flatiron Books for sharing this unconventional, unique ARC COPY with me in exchange my honest review.<br /><br /><a href="https://niluferozmekik.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/nilylovestoread/" rel="nofollow noopener">instagram</a><br /><a href="https://www.facebook.com/nilufer.ozmekik" rel="nofollow noopener">facebook</a><br /><a href="https://twitter.com/NiluferOzmekik" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11374446691940016338" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3414244858" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3414244858" />
    <a title="megs_bookrack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack"><img alt="megs_bookrack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532027727p2/48328025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3414244858?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="megs_bookrack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="megs_bookrack" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack">megs_bookrack</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3414244858" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13355620208923268786"><b>**4.5-stars**</b><br/><br/><i>‘Sometimes the Princess is a monster.’</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1593957136ra/29765599.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>Girl, Serpent, Thorn</i> is Melissa Bashardoust's sophomore novel; one I had been very highly anticipating.<br/><br/>Her debut, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32768509.Girls_Made_of_Snow_and_Glass' title='Girls Made of Snow and Glass by Melissa Bashardoust' rel='nofollow noopener'>Girls Made of Snow and Glass</a>, a wildly creative reimagining of <i>Snow White</i>, blew me away when I read it back in 2018. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1506452985ra/24019963.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I was astounded by her vivid imagination and ability to uniquely recreate a well-known tale.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551347318ra/27129335.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This latest story is an original fairy tale following a princess, Soraya, who due to a curse is poisonous to the touch. <br/><br/>Becaus</span>
  <span id="freeText13355620208923268786" style="display:none"><b>**4.5-stars**</b><br><br><i>‘Sometimes the Princess is a monster.’</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1593957136ra/29765599.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Girl, Serpent, Thorn</i> is Melissa Bashardoust's sophomore novel; one I had been very highly anticipating.<br><br>Her debut, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32768509.Girls_Made_of_Snow_and_Glass" title="Girls Made of Snow and Glass by Melissa Bashardoust" rel="nofollow noopener">Girls Made of Snow and Glass</a>, a wildly creative reimagining of <i>Snow White</i>, blew me away when I read it back in 2018. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1506452985ra/24019963.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I was astounded by her vivid imagination and ability to uniquely recreate a well-known tale.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551347318ra/27129335.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This latest story is an original fairy tale following a princess, Soraya, who due to a curse is poisonous to the touch. <br><br>Because of this, her family has kept her locked away, a secret hidden from the rest of the kingdom.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1601430989ra/30170209.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As she grows older, watching the world from high atop the castle, she begins to grow resentful. <br><br>Her brother, the Shah, is set to marry a girl she once considered her best friend; who was in fact, her only friend.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1593957136ra/29765600.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When circumstances arrive that bring a captured Div, a magical demon, into the castle’s dungeons, Soraya believes they may hold the answers she seeks. The cure for her curse. <br><br>Little does she know, that one bit of information could actually be the downfall for them all.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1584212615ra/29107338.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I really enjoyed this. Bashardoust’s writing continues to impress. <br><br>The world-building was fantastic and I loved the Persian atmosphere.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1593957136ra/29765601.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Although this is an original story, I could feel the influences from many other mythologies and fairy tales. I thought it was executed beautifully. <br><br>There were moments when I could see a bit of <i>Sleeping Beauty, Beauty and the Beast, Arabian Nights,</i> or <i>Rapunzel</i>, to name a few.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1601430989ra/30170210.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Although it is a story full of magical powers and beings, the writing didn’t suffer from trying to be overly whimsical. <br><br>I find with some stories, they try to up the magical feel in a way that ends up overshadowing the actual plot. That certainly wasn’t the case here!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452277589ra/17672368.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As Soraya discovers the truth of her curse, she begins to question her entire life, what she has been told and who she can trust. There was a lot of back and forth between different characters, where as the reader, you weren’t even sure who she could trust.<br><br>There were a few deep deceptions, a lot of plotting and a lot of monsters. The stakes were high and I was definitely cheering for Soraya the whole way through. She has a great arc over the course of the story as she grew in confidence and courage.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1593957136ra/29765602.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I would highly recommend this to YA Fantasy readers. If you are looking for a diverse Fantasy, Soraya is a bi-MC and the Persian influence can be felt throughout. I think this book really has something for everyone. <br><br>There is a lot more I could talk about with regards to the plot, it has plenty of depth and intricacies to explore, but I think it is best to go into the story knowing as little as possible.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491317068ra/22397461.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>You can enter this one confident you are in the hands of a skilled storyteller. Bashardoust has never let me down and I will continue to pick up anything she has published.<br><br>I would like to thank the publisher, Flatiron Books, for not only providing me with a copy of this read and review, but also including me on the blog tour for its release. It is an honor to be able to help promote Bashardoust and her beautiful stories!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1593957136ra/29765603.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="13355620208923268786" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <br>
  <br>
  <i>Stories always begin the same way. There was and there was not. There is a possibility in those words, the chance for hope or despair.</i>
</blockquote>Soraya is a princess but she has <b>spent her life in fairytales </b>and hidden away because of her deepest, darkest secret. <blockquote>
  <i>...the div cursed her firstborn daughter, making her poisonous, so that anyone who touched her would die.</i>
</blockquote>After a lifetime without touch, Soraya finds herself yearning ever-more for someone - anyone - to break her isolation.<br><br>When a div (demon) is taken into<b> the dungeons,</b> she finally realizes that she might have a chance to learn more about her curse and possibly break free...but she knows demons lie. <br><br>Is she willing to<b> risk it all </b>for a chance at freedom?<blockquote>
  <i>"Do you see now why I recognized you? You're my favorite story. I feel like I've known you for a long time."</i>
</blockquote>First of all - <b>GORGEOUS </b>cover on this one. I absolutely LOVED the color scheme, the roses, thorns and snakes. Really eye-catching.<br><br>I loved the concept of this book - the poisoned princess, the demon-in-the-dungeon, and the mysterious stranger who loves her. <br><br>The three major characters played well off of each other and had a pretty good balance between the three of them. There were a few moments that felt a bit predictable but overall I was entertained by the direction of the book.<br><br>The plot was interesting but it was missing a little sparkle. I think it's because we spend a lot of time inside or hiding, which is confining to astory.<br><br>The pacing felt a bit slow as Soraya waffled about whether she should take a plunge or stay in safety (which got...a little annoying after a bit) but once she finally made up her mind, the<b> plot took off like a rocket.</b><br><br>All in all, I quite liked this one and I'm looking forward to what the author writes next!<br><br><i>With thanks to Netgalley, Flatiron Books and Melissa Bashardoust for sending me a free copy in exchange for an honest review</i></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2139446703" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2139446703" />
    <a title="may ➹" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68157476-may"><img alt="may ➹" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538949856p2/68157476.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2139446703?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="may ➹" class="user" itemprop="url" name="may ➹" href="/user/show/68157476-may">may ➹</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=pretty-cover">pretty-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=rep-lgbtqiap">rep-lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=rep-poc-author">rep-poc-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=read-2020">read-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=pov-female">pov-female</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=pov-3rd">pov-3rd</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=rep-poc">rep-poc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=rep-poc-asian">rep-poc-asian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2139446703" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11659892087625567730">[slams hand on table] I wanted more GAY.<br/><br/>—★—<br/><br/>Girl, Serpent, Thorn is an <b>enthrallingly written fantasy drawing inspiration from Persian mythology and Sleeping Beauty</b>. Soraya, the twin sister of the Shah, should be able to walk the streets of her country freely and touch anything without the worry that it will wither away. But for her entire life, she has been cursed with a poisonous touch, with the blood of a div (demon) coursing through her. When a div is captured in a local village, Soraya may fi</span>
  <span id="freeText11659892087625567730" style="display:none">[slams hand on table] I wanted more GAY.<br /><br />—★—<br /><br />Girl, Serpent, Thorn is an <b>enthrallingly written fantasy drawing inspiration from Persian mythology and Sleeping Beauty</b>. Soraya, the twin sister of the Shah, should be able to walk the streets of her country freely and touch anything without the worry that it will wither away. But for her entire life, she has been cursed with a poisonous touch, with the blood of a div (demon) coursing through her. When a div is captured in a local village, Soraya may find the cure to her curse—or a threat that endangers her family and country.<br /><br />After reading the first few chapters, I was afraid that I might end up disappointed. There is a plot twist—though I’d say it is more like a plot reveal since it wasn’t particularly surprising—and when it happened, I feared that its obviousness would ruin the rest of the story for me. Fortunately, the remainder of the book <b>unfurls deliciously without as much predictability</b>.<br /><br />I flew through this book in a matter of only a few days. I remember staying up late in bed to read this, with only the warm light of my lamp and this immersive, twisting story to keep me company. Something about <b>Bashardoust’s writing is gripping and lends this book a classic fairytale feeling</b>. While I may have liked her previous book, Girls Made of Snow and Glass, more, I think her writing definitely improved in this one and it is utterly transportive.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>She had read enough stories to know that the princess and the monster were never the same. She had been alone long enough to know which one she was.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />Soraya was a fascinating character to follow throughout this book. She grapples with her inability to become close with anyone—from a fear that stems both from herself and everyone around her, a fear that she is nothing more than her curse and a blight on her family. Her <b>loneliness became a part of her, as did her feelings of shame and self-loathing</b>, and all of this only contributed to the questionable decisions she made.<br /><br />Honestly, I found myself wanting more from her—perhaps it’s the lady villain lover in me, but I just really would’ve loved to see her give in to the idea that she was a monster and relish in it. But that truly was an issue with my own personal taste, and I also realized that that isn’t the point of her character. Soraya is someone who is learning how to be herself and how to love herself after fearing what it means to be <i>Soraya</i>. And all of this growth happens as she gets closer to a villain that she can actually envision herself becoming, which just makes her development even better: <b>She explores her own monstrosity and reclaims what it means for her after having it defined by everyone her entire life.</b><br /><br />I also had the same issues with the side characters; I wanted to see more from both the villain and Parvaneh. They certainly didn’t feel two-dimensional and were both interesting characters, and I enjoyed learning more about them and their backgrounds. But for me, there was still something missing from them.<br /><br />Probably my biggest source of dismay was that <b>the romance between Soraya and Parvaneh did not deliver everything I wanted</b>, and I ached for more from it. I think this was due to the false advertising that this would be pretty focused on the f/f romance. While the romance <i>is</i> there (and it is wonderful and lovely and I adore it), it definitely wasn’t as central as I was expecting, and I really wish it had been. I felt the same way with Bashardoust’s previous book, so perhaps it is a stylistic choice of hers to not write too much romance in her books? But I think their relationship would have benefited from more development/scenes regardless—I loved the scenes between them and I simply wanted more sapphic goodness!!<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>She had thought nothing would be more incredible than the simple sensation of touch, but she’d been wrong: more incredible still was the idea that she could be dangerous, all her thorns on display, and that someone would dare to touch her anyway.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />Even though I don’t think the full potential of this book was reached, I still found it to be a captivating story, and I thought it was a <b>well-done exploration of loneliness, self-loathing, and the impacts of being raised to fear yourself</b>. If you’re looking for an entrancing fantasy that feels like a fairytale, with an antiheroine who goes on a journey to learn and love who she is, this book is for you! Unfortunately, I just wanted a little bit more from it.<br /><br />—★—<br /><br /><i><b>:: rep ::</b> Persian-coded cast, wlw MC (multi-gender attracted) and LI<br /><br /><b>:: content warnings ::</b> violence, murder/death, imprisonment, war, depictions/mentions of blood</i><br /><br /><blockquote>All quotes are taken from an advance copy and may differ in final publication.</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="11659892087625567730" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3078310249" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14027738407760819546"><i>"I am both the Sleeping Beauty and the enchanted castle; the princess drowses in the castle of her flesh."</i><br/><b>-Angela Carter</b>, <i>Vampirella</i><br/><br/>As someone who is new to Melissa Bashardoust's novels, I can't really say how this novel compares to her previous one, but what I can say is that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/51182650.Girl__Serpent__Thorn' title='Girl, Serpent, Thorn by Melissa Bashardoust' rel='nofollow noopener'>Girl, Serpent, Thorn</a> is a delightful breath of fresh air in the YA fantasy genre. I'm always on the search for fairytale retellings that incorporate non-Western stories, and this Persian inspired spin on "the poisonous gir</span>
  <span id="freeText14027738407760819546" style="display:none"><i>"I am both the Sleeping Beauty and the enchanted castle; the princess drowses in the castle of her flesh."</i><br><b>-Angela Carter</b>, <i>Vampirella</i><br><br>As someone who is new to Melissa Bashardoust's novels, I can't really say how this novel compares to her previous one, but what I can say is that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/51182650.Girl__Serpent__Thorn" title="Girl, Serpent, Thorn by Melissa Bashardoust" rel="nofollow noopener">Girl, Serpent, Thorn</a> is a delightful breath of fresh air in the YA fantasy genre. I'm always on the search for fairytale retellings that incorporate non-Western stories, and this Persian inspired spin on "the poisonous girl in the garden" was truly incredible.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1593003508ra/29700937.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It's really hard to touch on the plot, aside from what is shared in the synopsis, because there were many twists and turns that I wasn't expecting across the length of the book. Let's just say that secrets abound and characters can't always be trusted. Your emotions will be tested, not only by the (sort of) love triangle, but by Soraya's inner battles with the affliction that holds her. I cannot imagine not being able to touch or be touched by another soul, and I was intrigued by the physical and mental consequences that this brought on our main character. I think I'm going to stop here, and leave it up to you to decide if you'd like to read this story for yourself, but I'm really glad to have read this one, and I'm very interested in going back and picking up <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32768509.Girls_Made_of_Snow_and_Glass" title="Girls Made of Snow and Glass by Melissa Bashardoust" rel="nofollow noopener">Girls Made of Snow and Glass</a> while waiting for whatever she decides to write next.<br><br><i>*Many thanks to the publisher for providing my review copy via NetGalley.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="14027738407760819546" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3037682016" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3037682016" />
    <a title="Ꮗ€♫◗☿ ❤️ ilikebooksbest.com ❤️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70316517-ilikebooksbest-com"><img alt="Ꮗ€♫◗☿ ❤️ ilikebooksbest.com ❤️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570843185p2/70316517.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3037682016?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ꮗ€♫◗☿ ❤️ ilikebooksbest.com ❤️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ꮗ€♫◗☿ ❤️ ilikebooksbest.com ❤️" href="/user/show/70316517-ilikebooksbest-com">Ꮗ€♫◗☿ ❤️ ilikebooksbest.com ❤️</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/48510870-girl-serpent-thorn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70316517-ilikebooksbest-com?shelf=edelweiss-arc">edelweiss-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70316517-ilikebooksbest-com?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70316517-ilikebooksbest-com?shelf=fairytale">fairytale</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70316517-ilikebooksbest-com?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70316517-ilikebooksbest-com?shelf=lgbtqia">lgbtqia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3037682016" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9825044515382402810"><b>Dark, Unexpected and Completely Original!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1576637391ra/28629274.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1576637391ra/28629273.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This book was totally different than I thought it would be. I expected something along the lines of Rapunzel, with a princess locked away in a castle only to be rescued by a prince who is able to see who she really is despite her differences. However what I got was a girl who didn’t just sit in her room locked away and waiting to be rescued, but one who did what she could to rescue herself and she didn’t always do what was right or proper. She makes mista</span>
  <span id="freeText9825044515382402810" style="display:none"><b>Dark, Unexpected and Completely Original!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1576637391ra/28629274.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1576637391ra/28629273.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book was totally different than I thought it would be. I expected something along the lines of Rapunzel, with a princess locked away in a castle only to be rescued by a prince who is able to see who she really is despite her differences. However what I got was a girl who didn’t just sit in her room locked away and waiting to be rescued, but one who did what she could to rescue herself and she didn’t always do what was right or proper. She makes mistakes, big mistakes with far reaching effects. <br><br>I couldn’t always tell who was good and who was bad in this fairytale and it made it truly suspenseful and original. Soraya is the lead character and she is a twin to Sorush, the current Shah of Golvahar. She is cursed with poison in her veins and is unable to touch any living thing without killing it. She longs to get rid of her curse and be normal. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1576637391ra/28629275.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Her family travels every summer and she is left behind, only able to watch them return each fall from her tower where she is hidden away. After their return one season she sees a new face, among her brothers guard and looks to the tower and sees her as well. His name is Azad and he is a commoner that has become a royal guard because he saved the Shah when a div attacked him. Div’s are from Mount Arzur.<br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>Everyone there knew never to go wandering too close to the mountain, because it was the home of divs—the demonic servants of the Destroyer whose only purpose was to bring destruction and chaos to the Creator’s world.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><br>Soraya learns that the div that attacked her brother was caught and now resides in the dungeon. She believes that the div might have the answer to reversing her curse. Soraya uses the tunnels in the castle to sneak down and speak to the div. she meets Azad who helps her and she finds information that may help her. <br><br>I don’t want to give any more away than that. However Soraya, the div named Parvenah and Azad become entangled and what happens after that is quite a tale. There are many other characters is this story and the character development and world building is terrific. This was a dark fairytale with monsters, curses and evil, but the Soraya’s journey is quite different than I have seen in other fantasy novels and fairytales. Sometimes it is hard to tell if she is good or bad, and the same is true for many of the other characters.<br><br>Though it wasn’t the best I have read, it was definitely very good and worth reading. I have this book 4 stars for all the things I truly liked about it. I would definitely watch a movie of this one! I love fantasy and fairytales and this is one of the most original I have read, though it is a retelling. I’ve never heard the fairytale before. It is nice to see a flawed heroine, especially one as strong as Soraya!<br><br>I voluntarily read &amp; reviewed an advanced copy of this book. All thoughts &amp; opinions are my own.<br> <br><a href="https://www.ilikebooksbest.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a>|<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/wennel" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a>|<a href="https://www.facebook.com/ilikebooksbest" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a>|<a href="https://smile.amazon.com/gp/profile/amzn1.account.AFFE5A2BGXJQTQMCYHFC4YHV6KFQ?preview=true" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a>|<a href="https://www.twitter.com/wendysu020202" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a>|<a href="https://www.bookbub.com/profile/1895823057" rel="nofollow noopener">BookBub</a></span>

<div id="review_3079067640" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3079067640" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3079067640?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781529340976" href="/book/show/54127380-girl-serpent-thorn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=review-copies">review-copies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-ebooks">owned-ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-audio">owned-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=diverse-reads">diverse-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=soft-gay-babies">soft-gay-babies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3079067640" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8042968096555395315"><blockquote>
  <b>She had read enough stories to know that the princess and the monster were never the same. She had been alone long enough to know which one she was.</b>
</blockquote><br/>Friends, no matter how excited I was to read this gorgeous Persian fairytale retelling with queer girls and demons — a description that had all of my interests piqued entirely on its own — and no matter how many rave reviews I'd already seen, <i>nothing</i> could have prepared me for how utterly captivating and entrancing and gorgeous <i>Girl, Serpent, Tho</i></span>
  <span id="freeText8042968096555395315" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>She had read enough stories to know that the princess and the monster were never the same. She had been alone long enough to know which one she was.</b>
</blockquote><br />Friends, no matter how excited I was to read this gorgeous Persian fairytale retelling with queer girls and demons — a description that had all of my interests piqued entirely on its own — and no matter how many rave reviews I'd already seen, <i>nothing</i> could have prepared me for how utterly captivating and entrancing and gorgeous <i>Girl, Serpent, Thorn</i> was. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>Beautiful yet deadly, he had called her. Somehow, he made one sound as sweet as the other.</b>
</blockquote><br />First of all, the entire atmosphere and aesthetic of this story — please, this <i>has</i> to be made into a film, because I think it would be breathtaking. And the characters? They're genuinely complex, even some of the minor roles we don't see often, but don't even get me started on Soraya and Parvaneh, and how dear these two women are to my heart. Soraya is an incredibly three-dimensional protagonist with flaws and values, fears and desires, and my heart absolutely ached for her, all of the time — but don't get me wrong, she's tough as nails and a fierce protector, too. And Parvaneh? What I wouldn't give for a prequel novella about her before meeting Soraya! I'm such a sucker for demons as characters in the first place, but when you add in the complexities of the div types and the sisterhood of the parik, on top of Parvaneh's charm and general existence as a total badass? I, like Soraya, was doomed from the start.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>"There's something restless growing within you. We're all very curious to see what happens when it breaks free."</b>
</blockquote><br />As far as the <i>plot</i> goes, while the characters shone for me, I loved the entire storyline, too. I felt like Melissa Bashardoust took an arc that could've been dragged out into 2 or 3 books easily, yet she slimmed it down into just a few hundred pages without leaving me feeling as though anything was missing, and that's an incredible talent in my eyes. I couldn't get enough and the pacing kept me interested from cover to cover. I loved the exploration of Soraya's curse, but even more, I loved the familial aspect to it and her gradual understanding of why these things came into being. Nobody is innocent here, but everyone has a genuine motive, and it makes it hard to dislike any of these characters — even the villain.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"I've been expecting you. And you are very, very late."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />I also have to mention one particular plot point about three-quarters through that I won't spoil, but if you've read it, I'll just say a character is introduced who absolutely broke me. Watching Soraya reach this <i>depth</i> in understanding her ancestry, and the connection she is granted... It's hard to be vague here, because all I want to do is weep incoherently about how powerful the entire final act of this book was and how beautifully it all wrapped up.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b><i>If I am being cruel,</i> she decided, <i>then it's because he taught me how.</i></b>
</blockquote><br />I'll wrap this up in a moment, but finally, the discussion of betrayal and manipulation in <i>Girl, Serpent, Thorn</i> is so subtle and eloquent. Too often, we see princesses in fairytales who are tricked by wicked men and blame themselves, or are blamed by others; finally, Melissa Bashardoust has given us a princess who has been tricked and grows to recognize that she didn't <i>deserve</i> this behavior, and that <b>if her only fault was trusting a cruel man, the blame resides in his cruelty — not her kindness.</b> Truly, what an empowering story of hope and strength, and I know this one will stick with me for a long time to come.<br /><br />✨ <b>Representation:</b> <i>Girl, Serpent, Thorn</i> is inspired by the Persian epic <i>Shahnameh</i> and the author's exploration into her own culture. <b>Soraya</b> and <b>Parvaneh</b> are both queer (while Soraya is attracted to multiple genders in the context of the book, no labels are used for either character).<br /><br />✨ <b>Content warnings</b> for: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[violence, death, betrayal, manipulation, war, kidnapping, torture (in reference only) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><i>All quotes come from an advance copy and may not match the final release. Thank you so much to Flatiron Books for providing me with this ARC in exchange for an honest review!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="8042968096555395315" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3445061894" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5851116016595936944"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1594866641i/29821048._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Fairyloot's May 2020 Box - DESERT DREAMS 🖤<br/>My Rep Code: <a href='https://www.fairyloot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>MELANIE5</a> ❤️<br/><br/>Oh, I wanted to love this one so very badly! Sadly, most of the characters just felt so insufferable and their actions felt so convenient and questionable. This is ownvoices for the Persian mythos, and does star a bi MC (the author is queer, but I’m not sure what they ID as!) But this is a story about a princess who is cursed with a poisonous touch, and because of that she is constantly alone and locked away by her family because </span>
  <span id="freeText5851116016595936944" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1594866641i/29821048._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Fairyloot's May 2020 Box - DESERT DREAMS 🖤<br>My Rep Code: <a href="https://www.fairyloot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">MELANIE5</a> ❤️<br><br>Oh, I wanted to love this one so very badly! Sadly, most of the characters just felt so insufferable and their actions felt so convenient and questionable. This is ownvoices for the Persian mythos, and does star a bi MC (the author is queer, but I’m not sure what they ID as!) But this is a story about a princess who is cursed with a poisonous touch, and because of that she is constantly alone and locked away by her family because they don’t want anyone to know and she doesn’t want to hurt anyone on accident! That is, until she meets a boy named Azad who not only finds out but is not scared of her or her touch! You know, until bad things happen and her, her family, and her entire kingdom is in grave danger! <br><br>Now, this is where the insufferable MC comes in, because Soraya truly just makes the most questionable of choices, while the other characters just magically choose to believe her for progression of the story. Meanwhile, a demon girl named Pavenah is everything and I loved her with the sum of my being! <br><br>This had a lot of potential, and I liked the talk on power dynamics and imbalances a lot, but the story just never made me feel like there were any risks because they always conveniently worked out over and over again. Truly, even the villains in this book were the most trustworthy for no reason. Yet, I will say that I am very much in the minority with my feelings on this book, so maybe check out some other reviews! Also, I never want to read about convenient secret passages again either! <br><br><b>Content and Trigger Warnings:</b> blood, gore, violence, captivity, &amp; panic attack/anxiety depiction. <br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/jtotheimin" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://ko-fi.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Ko-fi</a> | <a href="https://open.spotify.com/user/meltotheany?si=kHJ5JnLHQsSp23fDe0qxSQ" rel="nofollow noopener">Spotify</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a><br><br>Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/33510193-romie" rel="nofollow noopener">Romie</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/76297785-ma-lys" rel="nofollow noopener">Maëlys</a>, &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/13507409-amy-risner" rel="nofollow noopener">Amy</a>! (we love an accidental <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/817630-dragons-tea-book-club" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragons &amp; Tea</a> buddy read!) ❤<br><br>❤ <a href="https://meltotheany.com/2020/07/20/2020-reading-rush-tbr/" rel="nofollow noopener">Reading Rush 2020</a></span>

<div id="review_3397690834" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3397690834" />
    <a title="Lucy Langford" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/74034800-lucy-langford"><img alt="Lucy Langford" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518091381p2/74034800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3397690834?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy Langford" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy Langford" href="/user/show/74034800-lucy-langford">Lucy Langford</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781529340976" href="/book/show/54127380-girl-serpent-thorn">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3397690834" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14206305785237485226"><i>”You could kill me with a single touch. Why should you ever be afraid of anyone?”</i><br/><br/>4.5****<br/><br/>This book was captivating and unexpected, filled with Persian mythology and culture. Our main protagonist, Soraya, the sister of the Shah, is cursed- she is poisonous to the touch causing almost instant death to most living and breathing things she touches. Living a life of exile in the palace, we witness her loneliness, jealousies and fear of her own power. <br/><br/>When Soraya hears that a Div has been captured, she</span>
  <span id="freeText14206305785237485226" style="display:none"><i>”You could kill me with a single touch. Why should you ever be afraid of anyone?”</i><br /><br />4.5****<br /><br />This book was captivating and unexpected, filled with Persian mythology and culture. Our main protagonist, Soraya, the sister of the Shah, is cursed- she is poisonous to the touch causing almost instant death to most living and breathing things she touches. Living a life of exile in the palace, we witness her loneliness, jealousies and fear of her own power. <br /><br />When Soraya hears that a Div has been captured, she immediately sets out to find answers about her curse and how to get rid of it. She also captures the attention of a new soldier along the way providing her with new opportunities to explore a whole new world outside the confines of the Palace. <br /><br />This wasn’t a romance book so much as a book of a character’s evolution and discovering her power. We witness everything from Soraya’s perspective; how she has jealousies, loneliness, anger, love. She is not the perfect princess that most fairytales portray, and this story instead shows her villainous side as well. <br /><br />This book features a bisexual heroine (which was a unique touch as this still does not always arise in YA fantasy) as she tries to navigate her feelings despite being cursed. This is her discovering the truth of the past, why she is cursed, and the awakenings and longings that arise outside of the Palace that she is kept in. <br /><br />I adored the use of Persian mythology in this. This is the first book that introduced me to Persian myths and I was fully immersed in reading it. This book also featured a girl who is poisonous to the touch which had me highly interested to read this book. <br /><br />This book had different twists and played out in ways that I did not predict- which was a nice surprise.<br /><br />A fantastic magical standalone!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14206305785237485226" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64075211-ellie-faerieontheshelf?shelf=stand-alone-novels">stand-alone-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64075211-ellie-faerieontheshelf?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64075211-ellie-faerieontheshelf?shelf=recieved-for-review">recieved-for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64075211-ellie-faerieontheshelf?shelf=antiheroes">antiheroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64075211-ellie-faerieontheshelf?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64075211-ellie-faerieontheshelf?shelf=ya-lit">ya-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64075211-ellie-faerieontheshelf?shelf=lgbtqia-sapphic">lgbtqia-sapphic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64075211-ellie-faerieontheshelf?shelf=own-voices">own-voices</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64075211-ellie-faerieontheshelf?shelf=lgbtqia-bi-pan">lgbtqia-bi-pan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64075211-ellie-faerieontheshelf?shelf=lgbtqia">lgbtqia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3144886095" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6611306788350118665">did someone summon me? I heard the magic words . . . <i>antiheroine arc and f/f and bisexual mc</i>.<br/><br/>The first thought I had immediately after finishing this (and throughout, really) is that I think it would have thrived as a duology. That is not to say it does not make a satisfying standalone (it does), but there are two identifiable parts to the book and I felt like the antiheroine arc could've been <i> really</i> good if pulled over two books, as would the development of the romance with Parvaneh. <br/><br/>The other</span>
  <span id="freeText6611306788350118665" style="display:none">did someone summon me? I heard the magic words . . . <i>antiheroine arc and f/f and bisexual mc</i>.<br /><br />The first thought I had immediately after finishing this (and throughout, really) is that I think it would have thrived as a duology. That is not to say it does not make a satisfying standalone (it does), but there are two identifiable parts to the book and I felt like the antiheroine arc could've been <i> really</i> good if pulled over two books, as would the development of the romance with Parvaneh. <br /><br />The other thing was that I kind of wished it was a lot darker. There is a clear antiheroine bent to Soraya, and sometimes she slips into a crueller mindset, but most of the time there's regret and hurt at how people treat her and at points I was honestly like RISE UP AND BECOME A DARK QUEEN WITH THE SHAHMAR. She also never really had that manipulative or morally grey bent I like to see in my antiheroines, but then again, her true purpose was not to go out and amass power for herself <s>even though I kind of wish it was but lol</s>. She was, in a way, a reluctant antiheroine who wanted to belong rather than feel like she was remotely evil in anyway. <br /><br />This kind of leads me onto the Shahmar, who I . . . loved? I actually saw the entire twist in the middle of the book coming when it was revealed that <i>that</i> character was actually the cursed snake king. You don't usually build up a romance with a character early on unless you're going to have a big twist in the middle of the story. And besides, aforementioned character was too nice and the foreshadowing with viper comparisons was there right in the beginning. For some readers, I do think it'll be a fun surprise though <s>unless you read this review in which I'm trying to be vague but you'll know when you start reading who I'm on about, rip.</s> <br /><br />I don't want to write tons about the Shahmar (okay maybe I do), but as a villain I really liked him. I love seeing villains explored and working as a kind of mirror to the hero/antihero, and that's done here. "You and I don't belong fully to either world," the Shahmar says to Soraya, and I'm a sucker for the cursed prince, the villian with understandable but flawed motivations. His actions towards Soraya were strangely kind, as he believed he finally had met someone who saw and understood and was just like him. In fact, because he was weirdly nice to Soraya throughout he sometimes didn't even seem like a big evil villain and look, I shipped it. Again, that's my own enjoyment of villian love interests coming in; he wanted someone to understand him and I'm a bit weak for that. Because of that, I was hoping, perhaps, for some kind of resolution or atonement for him at the ending. He cut Soraya a lot of slack when I thought it seemed clear she was acting against him, and when he assumed power, there was not a mass slaughter and the onset of a reign of utter terror. This kind of complexity in both villain and antiheroine characters is something Barshadoust does really well: it brings to mind Mina from her prior book, GIRLS MADE OF SNOW AND GLASS (who was my favourite character from that book, unsurprisingly.)<br /><br />I realise I haven't talked a lot about Parvaneh, but yay for monster girlfriends! I did like her, yes, and I liked her romance with Soraya and yay for f/f honestly, but I don't feel deeply invested in Soraya x Parvaneh like I do with my favourite f/f couples. There was nothing wrong with the development of Soraya &amp; Parvaneh's relationship (it was primarily moved into the second half of the book and didn't have that slow torturous unwind that I love in romances, tbf), but I also didn't really know enough about Parvaneh to feel closely connected to her beyond a superficial level and that affected how much enjoyment I took from things. I feel like I know more about the Shahmar than I know about Parvaneh, really. Again, this could have been solved if this novel was split into a duology and the development of the sapphic romance was given time to expand in the second book, but hmm. <br /><br />To be honest, for a standalone that's not overly long (just over 300 pages for my arc), GIRL, SERPENT, THORN is cohesive and well-developed. Not extensively, and like I said I wish it had been split into two books and the antiheroine potential of Soraya examined more, but Barshadoust has done really well in including it all. It works. It doesn't feel underdeveloped. The pacing is great. I loved the worldbuilding, and Soraya's rose garden. The Sleeping Beauty influences are minimal, but there are clear ones towards the end. I would definitely recommend it for people looking for a #ownvoices Persian fantasy.<br /><br />In addition, this book is my favourite book with snakes on the cover so far, besides NINTH HOUSE. I mean, LOOK AT IT. The white snake, the pink flowers, the thorns, the clean minimalism that is beautiful . . . yes. <br /><br /><b> &gt; 4 stars</b><br /><br /><i>I received an arc from the publisher in exchange for an honest review </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="6611306788350118665" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/79515542-emetis?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3110677199" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16351300828176541240">Buddy read with the amazing @Naomi Waters!!! I loved reading this book with you! <br/><br/><br/><br/>There was and there was not. A girl living in a castle hidden away like a secret or a treasure. Most people didn’t know about the Shahzadeh, the Shah’s twin sister. And there was a good reason for that, for the girl was cursed. Everything she touched was meant to die, for she was poisonous. <br/><br/><br/>I’m so emotional right now. This book means everything to me. As someone who comes from Iran reading a book about my own cultur</span>
  <span id="freeText16351300828176541240" style="display:none">Buddy read with the amazing @Naomi Waters!!! I loved reading this book with you! <br /><br /><br /><br />There was and there was not. A girl living in a castle hidden away like a secret or a treasure. Most people didn’t know about the Shahzadeh, the Shah’s twin sister. And there was a good reason for that, for the girl was cursed. Everything she touched was meant to die, for she was poisonous. <br /><br /><br />I’m so emotional right now. This book means everything to me. As someone who comes from Iran reading a book about my own culture, tradition, and myths was something that I didn’t know I needed in my life until I came across this book. <br />Yes, I have read books about my culture in persian but to read it in a language that is not my mother tongue, knowing that other people are also able to read it and get a glimpse of what my culture is like... that just made me so happy.<br />I know that there are other books written by Persian authors in English but so far non of them have stuck out to me the way this one has.<br /><br />The author has indeed done her research on the mythological aspect of this book. Most of the creatures come from the Shahnameh. And as someone who began reading the Shahnameh at a young age, I can tell you that the myths and the creatures are 100% accurate. <br /><br />The culture representation was my favorite thing about this book and to be honest, that’s the main reason why the moment I opened it, it became my all time favorite.<br />All those festivities, colors and food... they made me so nostalgic. <br /><br /><br />Parvaneh is by far my favorite character. She was so fascinating to read about and I loved her the moment she appeared. I loved how complex her character was. <br />I loved how she willingly sacrificed herself in order to save Soraya’s family. <br /><br />Although, in the end Soraya did come close to being my favorite!<br />The one thing I love about Soraya the most, is that she is unlike other female heroines. She isn’t trained in combat and she isn’t particularly clever. There is just something about her, that although I can’t find the right words to describe it right now, I loved about her.<br />Her character development was my favorite. In the beginning she said that the poison in her veins was a curse and in the end she embraced it.<br />Oh, and did I mention that she is Bisexual?<br />What a queen!<br /><br />The romance was very well done. It wasn’t rushed, it was a slow burn in fact. And I loved every second of reading about Parvaneh and Soraya. This book is by far one of my favorite books with a f|f romance.<br /><br /><br />And Azad...<br />In the end I kinda pitied him to be honest. That’s the thing with this book. Most of the characters are morally gray.<br />Even if he did do some questionable things, I believe that there was still some good in him.</span>

<div id="review_3077217433" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3077217433?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fadwa (Word Wonders)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fadwa (Word Wonders)" href="/user/show/42662881-fadwa-word-wonders">Fadwa (Word Wonders)</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3077217433" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16284615457427484154"><i>I received an earc of this book from the publisher in exchange of an honest review</i><br/><br/><b>CW: manipulation, murder, death, battle, intrusive thoughts.</b><br/><br/>Since the day I finished Girls Made of Snow and Glass by Melissa Bashardoust, I have been looking forward to whatever book she’ll be putting out next. So knowing the premise of Girl, Serpent, Thorn combined with how much I adore her writing I really couldn’t see how anything could go wrong with this book. And I was 110% right, Girl, Serpent, Thorn sucked m</span>
  <span id="freeText16284615457427484154" style="display:none"><i>I received an earc of this book from the publisher in exchange of an honest review</i><br /><br /><b>CW: manipulation, murder, death, battle, intrusive thoughts.</b><br /><br />Since the day I finished Girls Made of Snow and Glass by Melissa Bashardoust, I have been looking forward to whatever book she’ll be putting out next. So knowing the premise of Girl, Serpent, Thorn combined with how much I adore her writing I really couldn’t see how anything could go wrong with this book. And I was 110% right, Girl, Serpent, Thorn sucked me in from the first page, took me on a whirlwind of an emotional journey and I loved every second of it.<br /><br />The most accurate way I can think of to describe Melissa Bashardoust’s writing is that it reads like a fairytale. That was the case with her debut and this sophomore novel proved to be no different. All of this to say that the writing still is jaw-droppingly beautiful, with many quotable lines. It’s also atmospheric and enchanting with just the slightest hint of a dark eerie feel to it, it transports you to the world of the book with the lush descriptions, makes you feel every single emotion the main character experiences and gets you invested in everything happening. The lore in this book is also so rich but equally easy to understand and to immerse yourself into. Everything was well thought out and meticulously put together, no element of it was vague or left to chance.<br /><br />The way I like to pitch Girl, Serpent, Thorn is “Persian inspired fairytale with a morally grey main character and monster girlfriends” and although that sums up the key elements of the story of the story, this book is so much more. At it’s core, it’s a story that explores loneliness and the way it can affect people, the way isolation can mess with anyone’s head, the way secrets fester, grow and keeping them, even with the best intentions can do much more harm than good. And how all of this eats at a person’s soul until they start wondering if there’s anything of them left, and if there is, if any of it is worth keeping. And that character exploration was my favorite thing about the book.<br /><br />Read my full review on my blog <a href="https://wordwoonders.wordpress.com/2020/07/08/blog-tour-girl-serpent-thorn-morally-grey-characters-and-monster-girlfriends/" rel="nofollow noopener">Word Wonders</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16284615457427484154" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3031487468" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3031487468" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3031487468?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2020">read-2020</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3031487468" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14030671356690828251">This is a whimsical and fantastical Persian inspired fantasy and after finishing it, I totally <i>get</i> the cover now. The whole book is this balance of bloody thorns and monstrous hearts, mixed together with beauty and innocence and aching loneliness. It's based on quite a few threads of mythology like Rappaccini's Daughter, the Persian epic Shahnameh, and a bit of Sleeping Beauty mixed in. It also felt a lot like the Ballad of Tamlin I think? (Basically if you liked ACTOAR but wished it was gay; th</span>
  <span id="freeText14030671356690828251" style="display:none">This is a whimsical and fantastical Persian inspired fantasy and after finishing it, I totally <i>get</i> the cover now. The whole book is this balance of bloody thorns and monstrous hearts, mixed together with beauty and innocence and aching loneliness. It's based on quite a few threads of mythology like Rappaccini's Daughter, the Persian epic Shahnameh, and a bit of Sleeping Beauty mixed in. It also felt a lot like the Ballad of Tamlin I think? (Basically if you liked ACTOAR but wished it was gay; this is for you.) I also loved the exploration of the div (demon) lore.<br /><br />I always crave more sapphic fantasy so I loved that about it! Soraya is probably bisexual (obviously no labels on page) and her sexuality wasn't a big deal?! It just was. And I loved that. Parvaneh is a <i>Parik</i> (type of demon) and Soraya has been cursed with poison running through her veins. Everything she touches dies. There's this comparison of: who really is the monster. And Soraya is so lonely and touch-starved, which makes her pretty naive but understandably so? My regret is that Parvaneh and Soraya actually have very little page time together. I feel their relationship could've been much deeper.<br /><br />Overall it's a fantasy both beautiful and monstrous, easy to read, and steeped in Persian folklore and culture -- with some super compelling plot twists too 👀👀</span>
  <a data-text-id="14030671356690828251" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
