        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3192309128" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer6445779894614365892">This was fun! I didn't have super high expectations going in because YA fantasy isn't typically my favorite genre, but this was pretty fun to read. It wasn't a perfect story, and I do think that A LOT of the conflicts had very convenient and easy solutions, but overall this was a fun time and I'm happy that I spent the last few days in between these pages. I did end up listening to this one as an audiobook while reading along in the physical book and I think that added to the experience for me. </span>
  <span id="freeText6445779894614365892" style="display:none">This was fun! I didn't have super high expectations going in because YA fantasy isn't typically my favorite genre, but this was pretty fun to read. It wasn't a perfect story, and I do think that A LOT of the conflicts had very convenient and easy solutions, but overall this was a fun time and I'm happy that I spent the last few days in between these pages. I did end up listening to this one as an audiobook while reading along in the physical book and I think that added to the experience for me. I liked the narrator and listening to this really made it feel more like getting told a fairy tale and I am not mad about it. Definitely recommend if you want to read a fairy tale-esque queer fantasy!</span>

<div id="review_3061570148" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3061570148" />
    <a title="Vee_Bookish // YA Book Blogger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67389898-vee-bookish-ya-book-blogger"><img alt="Vee_Bookish // YA Book Blogger" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603583342p2/67389898.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3061570148?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vee_Bookish // YA Book Blogger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vee_Bookish // YA Book Blogger" href="/user/show/67389898-vee-bookish-ya-book-blogger">Vee_Bookish // YA Book Blogger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781250196156" href="/book/show/51184707-girl-serpent-thorn">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3061570148" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8435510248397053597">I'm also a book blogger: <a href='https://vee-bookish.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Vee_Bookish</a><br/>(ARC provided by NetGalley, my opinions are unbiased)<br/><br/>This was one of two books I read at the same time, that I found difficult to finish because I was just so incredibly bored (the other one was Havenfall). Originally I thought that this may because we've just hit the Coronavirus epidemic, but after finishing the books I realised that they both have major issues that affected my reading.<br/><br/>This book sounded so, so good with hella Medusa vibes. It's based around P</span>
  <span id="freeText8435510248397053597" style="display:none">I'm also a book blogger: <a href="https://vee-bookish.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Vee_Bookish</a><br />(ARC provided by NetGalley, my opinions are unbiased)<br /><br />This was one of two books I read at the same time, that I found difficult to finish because I was just so incredibly bored (the other one was Havenfall). Originally I thought that this may because we've just hit the Coronavirus epidemic, but after finishing the books I realised that they both have major issues that affected my reading.<br /><br />This book sounded so, so good with hella Medusa vibes. It's based around Persian mythology about a princess that cannot touch anyone cos they drop dead, presumably dramatically. It sounded cool as hell and I wanted to read it for a couple of months before it made an appearance on NetGalley.<br /><br />This just did not have the kick that I wanted. Like many readers, I'm tired of woe-is-me main characters that spend most of their books moping about how hard their lives are. I'm sorry, it just doesn't make for interesting reading. This character is supposed to be embracing her darker and lighter sides and she just came across as pathetic. And really, really annoying.<br /><br />The plot was both fairly easy to guess and overcomplicated, as well as all over the place. The various demons needed a full colour illustrated guide because I could not picture them in the slightest. The plot weirdly reminded me of Labyrinth in some places and it's really hard to discuss it's issues without giving major spoilers, as the second half is where everything happens and the first half is Soraya just mooching about the castle, moping about the one time she poked a butterfly and it died.<br /><br />Azad? Annoying and almost cartoonish. Soraya? Annoying. Parvaneh? Honestly kinda cool, the book would have been better from her perspective. The world building... honestly outside of Soraya's immediate area I have zero clue how that world functions and the harmony between the creatures and humans (or lack of it) is kinda glossed over. It was an interesting book with maybe a few too many things thrown at it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8435510248397053597" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11179133573357276247"><u>Star Rating</u>:<i> —></i> <b>4.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>Well, I have to say I was a bit nervous going into this, given the mixed reviews and total GR rating being just under 4 stars (which btw this confounds me— I truly believe this deserves AT LEAST 4 solid stars, but 🤷🏼‍♀️) ... <br/><br/><b>I have to say, though, that this was absolutely magical, fantastic & <i>everything my mythology/folklore loving heart could’ve asked for</i>! Such an awesome look into Persian mythology</b>, which is one culture whose folklore tales I was not at all familiar wi</span>
  <span id="freeText11179133573357276247" style="display:none"><u>Star Rating</u>:<i> —&gt;</i> <b>4.5 Stars</b><br /><br />Well, I have to say I was a bit nervous going into this, given the mixed reviews and total GR rating being just under 4 stars (which btw this confounds me— I truly believe this deserves AT LEAST 4 solid stars, but 🤷🏼‍♀️) ... <br /><br /><b>I have to say, though, that this was absolutely magical, fantastic &amp; <i>everything my mythology/folklore loving heart could’ve asked for</i>! Such an awesome look into Persian mythology</b>, which is one culture whose folklore tales I was not at all familiar with before this novel.<br /><br />It was very much told in a beautiful, atmospheric, &amp; layered fairytale format and I loved every second of it— it was <i>utterly transportive</i>!<br />The plot consistently keeps you on your toes, twist after twist, &amp; deception after deception; you literally never know who you could actually trust— sometimes even the main character, Soraya, was suspect!<br /><b> Soraya is very much a morally grey character &amp; I dig that SOMUCH</b>. <br /><i>Give me a complex, morally grey character any day, any time, anywhere.</i><br /><br />Plus <b>Soraya &amp; Parvaneh</b>... ahhh <b>BE STILL MY HEART</b>; so <u>
  <i>COMPLETELY in love with some queer romance in this wonderful fairytale</i>
</u>. <br /><br />I know this brief, I but I do not want to spoil anything about this wonderful, wonderful myth-like fairytale. I <i>truly loved this dark romp in Persian mythology from start to finish</i>. <br /><br /><u>I highly recommend this</u> to any <b>fantasy lover</b>, <b>world mythologies lover</b>, <b>fairytale lover</b>, &amp; well, <i>
  <b>anyone at all</b>
</i> !<br /><br /><b>10/ 10 Recommend!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="11179133573357276247" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3153857818?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittany Lee {Healing Happy}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittany Lee {Healing Happy}" href="/user/show/76006819-brittany-lee-healing-happy">Brittany Lee {Healing Happy}</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76006819-brittany-lee-healing-happy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3153857818" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15955385143381971979">Sweet and beautiful like a rose on the outside, prickly thorns line the inside. <b>This is a fairytale gone rogue.</b> She is a princess, she is a monster...<br/><br/>GIRL, SERPENT, THORN is a queer (female/female/bi) YA fantasy inspired by Persian mythology, the American fairytales- SLEEPING BEAUTY, RAPUNZEL, and RAPPACCINI'S DAUGHTER, and the author's exploration of legends and myths of her own culture and heritage, with particular attention tributed to the Persian- Sasanian era.<br/><br/>All of the historical words for</span>
  <span id="freeText15955385143381971979" style="display:none">Sweet and beautiful like a rose on the outside, prickly thorns line the inside. <b>This is a fairytale gone rogue.</b> She is a princess, she is a monster...<br /><br />GIRL, SERPENT, THORN is a queer (female/female/bi) YA fantasy inspired by Persian mythology, the American fairytales- SLEEPING BEAUTY, RAPUNZEL, and RAPPACCINI'S DAUGHTER, and the author's exploration of legends and myths of her own culture and heritage, with particular attention tributed to the Persian- Sasanian era.<br /><br />All of the historical words foreign to me were in a different language (Persian) and described briefly in the context of the story, but also defined thoroughly in the author's note at the end of the book. There weren't too many foreign words, but they make a bold statement. I enjoyed learning terms in the Persian language, such as calling demons- divs (pronounced DEEVS) and calling the New Year- Nog Roz. They were easy to remember and fun to come across.<br /><br />I admired Melissa Bashardoust's spin on the folklore. It was well written, keeping me engaged the entire time! The story kept twisting and turning, continuously keeping the suspense high, I loved all the action that was going on! I couldn't wait to see what was happening next. The characters had depth and real emotions.<br /><br /><i>"I think you have so much power within you that it scares you, and that you make yourself small on purpose because you don't know what you'll become if you ever stop."</i><br /><br />The storytelling through the imagery of roses, thorns, scales, poison, incense, divs, mythology, emotions, and characters, it was all so VIVID. Highly imaginative and gorgeous scenery! The magical elements were incredibly creative.<br /><br /><i>"Was she destined always to grow close to people who would betray her? Or perhaps the problem was that she wasn't growing close to people, but to demons."</i><br /><br />As someone who doesn't normally read the fantasy genre, I was shocked by how much I liked this. I love retellings of fairytales/folklore, anything with monsters, demons, villain-ery, and heroism. I guess it's safe to say that I like a very limited amount of fantasy. I'm happy to add this one to the collection.<br /><br />This was more than just a pretty cover! I expect this book to be a HUGE success. It was magical, thrilling, and sweet. <br /><br />Much gratitude to the publisher Flatiron Books, compliments of the Goodreads Giveaway Program for the paperback ARC I received. I was under no obligation to write a review, my honest opinion is freely given. The quotes I chose may not reflect the final publication, as the author may have made changes prior to print.</span>

<div id="review_3250893340" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3250893340" />

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="anna (½ of readsrainbow)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="anna (½ of readsrainbow)" href="/user/show/8645302-anna-of-readsrainbow">anna (½ of readsrainbow)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8645302-anna-of-readsrainbow?shelf=pub-2020">pub-2020</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8645302-anna-of-readsrainbow?shelf=5-young-adult">5-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8645302-anna-of-readsrainbow?shelf=1-fantasy">1-fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3250893340" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12068365889483770942"><b>rep:</b> Persian cast & settings, bi mc, sapphic li<br/><br/><b>Review also on <a>my blog</a>. <i>ARC provided by the publisher</i>.</b><br/><br/><i>Girl, Serpent, Thorn</i> is revolutionary in more than one respect and for that we should all be grateful. It’s a feminist fairy tale for the modern times, even though it’s set in ancient Persia, even though it’s full of magic and monsters. <br/><br/>The plot is influenced by <i>Sleeping Beauty</i>, but at every turn twists the the well known story into something new and unexpected, and extraordinary. The princess is</span>
  <span id="freeText12068365889483770942" style="display:none"><b>rep:</b> Persian cast &amp; settings, bi mc, sapphic li<br /><br /><b>Review also on <a>my blog</a>. <i>ARC provided by the publisher</i>.</b><br /><br /><i>Girl, Serpent, Thorn</i> is revolutionary in more than one respect and for that we should all be grateful. It’s a feminist fairy tale for the modern times, even though it’s set in ancient Persia, even though it’s full of magic and monsters. <br /><br />The plot is influenced by <i>Sleeping Beauty</i>, but at every turn twists the the well known story into something new and unexpected, and extraordinary. The princess isn’t a damsel in distress, she’s a monster and it is she, who does most of the saving. “The evil witch” learns new tricks and gets a backstory. The prince? There’s no prince in this fairy tale; who needs him, when you have a group of women who love each other and would sacrifice everything for one another?<br /><br />The titular girl (who is also a serpent and a thorn) is poisonous and her curse literally makes it so that anyone who touches her, dies. Not only is that terribly romantic and a great premise for a story, it’s also an incredible concept for a girl character. A young girl who doesn’t have to worry about men touching her without consent? A young girl who doesn’t have to feel afraid of men around her? It’s quite frankly groundbreaking. <br /><br />The most obvious change between the folk tale and <i>Girl, Serpent, Thorn</i> is the moment the princess falls asleep. They both prick themselves on a finger and draw blood, but the first (original) one does it unknowingly, while Soraya soughts that ending out. And no, she doesn’t magically fall asleep for a hundred years, but it’s a close thing, with the way she loses a vital part of herself in that process. <br /><br /><i>Girl, Serpent, Thorn</i> isn’t just a retelling of a fairy tale, though. It adds so much to the story, they’re more like cousins thrice removed. And what makes it the most unique, is the Persian setting. Bashardoust created a magical, rich gold world inspired by her own cultural history and the love she poured into it is visible in every little detail.<br /><br />If you’re looking for a diverse feminist story with a cast of strong yet flawed women, and an intense sapphic relationship at the heart of it, you should definitely start reading <i>Girl, Serpent, Thorn</i> right this second.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12068365889483770942" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucie V." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucie V." href="/user/show/84801697-lucie-v">Lucie V.</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84801697-lucie-v?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3232746595" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11082852153011177202">3.5 stars <br/><br/>Soraya was cursed by a demon when she was only a baby: anyone who touches her dies instantly. She has spent her life hidden away so she wouldn't tarnish the royal family's reputation (she is the Shah's twin sister after all) or accidentally kill someone and now more than ever, she yearns for warmth and touch. She wants more than this sad isolated life where even her family does not really know her or talk to her. It all seems hopeless until a div (demon) is taken prisoner and brought t</span>
  <span id="freeText11082852153011177202" style="display:none">3.5 stars <br /><br />Soraya was cursed by a demon when she was only a baby: anyone who touches her dies instantly. She has spent her life hidden away so she wouldn't tarnish the royal family's reputation (she is the Shah's twin sister after all) or accidentally kill someone and now more than ever, she yearns for warmth and touch. She wants more than this sad isolated life where even her family does not really know her or talk to her. It all seems hopeless until a div (demon) is taken prisoner and brought to the palace. Soraya learns that the only way for her to get rid of her curse would mean betraying her family. Now she needs to decide if a chance at freedom is really worth it.<br /><br />The characters in this book are great. Soraya is a complex girl with loads of emotions (good and bad). She spent her life in isolation so she is a bit naive and she wants to be able to touch other people so much that it might lead her to bad decisions, but on the other side, she is not stupid enough to throw everything away simply for a pretty smile. The other two more important characters are also well developed and they bring different aspects of Soraya to light. We can see her grow from a girl who is afraid and tormented by the poison in her veins to a determined and brave woman.<br /><br />The world-building remains basic, but the story focuses more on the characters so it does not affect the quality of the plot. There is action, deception, and betrayal and also a hint of romance, and all in all it is well balanced.<br /><br />The beginning of the story is a little slow, maybe because Soraya spent so much time hiding inside, wondering what to do, but once she made up her mind the pace picked up and the rest of the book was very enjoyable.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11082852153011177202" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3473176705" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13828437336716756959">One of the most mind-blowing mixed novel I've ever read, GST is a retelling story of a Persian fairytale merged with demons and queer girls! Bashardoust has written one of the most captivating story which has amazed me and not that I liked the whole story but it definitely is in my top 5 YA reads of all time! <br/>.<br/>The background structure of the World is intriguing filled with many fascinating details that will drown you into imagination! Soraya is the main character who is a three dimensional chara</span>
  <span id="freeText13828437336716756959" style="display:none">One of the most mind-blowing mixed novel I've ever read, GST is a retelling story of a Persian fairytale merged with demons and queer girls! Bashardoust has written one of the most captivating story which has amazed me and not that I liked the whole story but it definitely is in my top 5 YA reads of all time! <br />.<br />The background structure of the World is intriguing filled with many fascinating details that will drown you into imagination! Soraya is the main character who is a three dimensional character, her emotions are extremely powerful and complexed, she builds in a very compelling and enjoyable person that everyone wants to know more about! The entire storyline is so rich in prose and does not leave you alone with the intriguing and intense performances of the characters!<br />.<br />Empowering story of a Princess that talks about the right struggles and gives us a new strategy of a fairytale to believe and give our hopes on! Soraya presents hope, desire and strength within these pages and she truly is an inspiration to all of us!<br />Melissa is an incredible writer as she has merged violence, betrayal, curse and manipulation in these pages in some way that noone could, she is outstanding wonderfully completed Author!<br />.<br />The fantastical fantasy has perforated beyond my imagination, I can totally say that this book is unique but if you want a background of the previous works that you might've seen/read this is if Princess Aurora met ACOTAR! But despite the fact that this one is more detailed and has more modern backgrounds!<br />.<br />The chemistry between Soraya and Pavenah was something special and beyond perfection, I loved their parts together and I felt so much emotions! <br />Soraya has to choose between some incredibly difficult choices about her life, and the enthusiasm always gets a place in these tough situations! Also Azad is a compulsive character with a detailed personality, I enjoyed him too as we get to discover their stories! <br />.<br />The folklore performances and melted myths within the pages have created such a masterpiece that has blown our minds but have stayed in our hearts, we loved Girl, Serpent, Thorn nore that I ever imagined and I highly recommend you to read this wonderful book which has an extremely gorgeous cover which will be explained through the pages!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13828437336716756959" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3184934446" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3184934446" />
    <a title="Sara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1170391-sara"><img alt="Sara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590218363p2/1170391.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3184934446?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara" href="/user/show/1170391-sara">Sara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781529340976" href="/book/show/54127380-girl-serpent-thorn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3184934446" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7798689283581711659">ARC received in exchange for an honest review<br/><br/>Fairyloot May Book of the Month 2020<br/><br/>Soraya is a princess cursed to be poisonous to the touch. Hidden away from the rest of her family, and the wider world, she must learn to step out of the shadows of her torment in order to protect her kingdom after she makes a terrible mistake. By her side is Azad, the handsome guardian who is unafraid of Soraya’s deadly touch, and whose eyes linger on her deadly potential. On her other side is the mysterious Pavena</span>
  <span id="freeText7798689283581711659" style="display:none">ARC received in exchange for an honest review<br /><br />Fairyloot May Book of the Month 2020<br /><br />Soraya is a princess cursed to be poisonous to the touch. Hidden away from the rest of her family, and the wider world, she must learn to step out of the shadows of her torment in order to protect her kingdom after she makes a terrible mistake. By her side is Azad, the handsome guardian who is unafraid of Soraya’s deadly touch, and whose eyes linger on her deadly potential. On her other side is the mysterious Pavenah, a demon with moth wings who may hold the answers to lifting her curse, but will pull her into the darkness to do so.<br /><br />I really enjoyed the dynamics between the three main characters. Pavenah and Soraya have a great chemistry that simmers with heated looks and sensual touches. She’s the living embodiment of how Soraya sees herself – a monster like those depicted in the myths and legends told throughout her kingdom. But Pavenah is happy as she is – she’s strong, powerful and beautiful and it’s only when Soraya starts to see this in Pavenah that she starts to understand it in herself. By comparison, Azad is the stereotypical handsome hero who wants to protect and shield Soraya. Although he sees her inner fire, he nurtures this anger into his manipulation of her character. He tries to shape her into what she always wanted to be, rather than what she should be. The two are the light and dark of Soraya’s personality, and it was interesting to watch the dynamics between them shift continuously as the story progresses and Soraya struggles internally to decide on the right path.<br /><br />Soraya’s character is definitely a highlight to this novel. I found her very well developed, with a lot of internal conversations about what the right thing to do is. She has grown up her whole life isolated from everyone and everything, living her life through the people she sees from her palace rooftop, and as a result she’s a very lonely woman at the start of the story. She’s also envious, jealous of her brother’s soon to be bride who will remain in the limelight with her brother while she’ll be forced back into the shadows. She wants to prove herself, prove her worth and there’s a lot of philosophical discussions about whether the hunt for a cure for Soraya’s curse is actually turning her into more of a monster than the actual curse itself because of a few rather ‘choice’ decisions she makes. She’s an extremely interesting character.<br /><br />I also loved the rich descriptions of the lush settings and the small hints we get at the wider world and its mythology were utterly captivating. It’s based on Persian mythology, and I loved the inclusion of old heroic stories told by Soraya to help shape the story and I liked the way these stories eventually intertwine with Soraya’s tale. However, I do wish that more time had been spent expanding this world. We get far too few glimpses into the various demons (known as divs) who live in the world, and we’re never really given an explanation into any sort of social constructs or hierarchy between them, except that the group Pavenah belongs too may be classed as intelligent winged spies. Some groups appear to be merely grunts, with a few well known individuals with given names and ‘specialities’ (such as a zombie type div who specialises in the dead), and I would have liked to have seen more of the history behind this.<br /><br />I also found the pacing a bit off. The first 100 pages are rather slow and meandering, with very little in the way of plot development. However, after this point there’s a major plot twist and the action just keeps coming – to the point where the ending feels rushed and a little bit too neatly tied up, too quickly. Soraya seems to be able to overcome her many difficulties rather too conveniently.<br /><br />That said, I found the characters and setting for this to be truly magical and unique. Soraya is a complex, well thought out protagonist and there are some interesting dynamics between her, Azad and Pavenah that I haven’t really seen before. If you enjoy YA fantasy, I would highly recommend this for an interesting new take on the genre that includes some wonderful Persian mythology.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7798689283581711659" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6614387245533752477"><i> The ARC of this book was provided by the publisher via NetGalley in exchange for an honest review. </i><br/><br/>Full review <a href='https://booksrealwhenshared.wordpress.com/2020/07/11/girl-serpent-thorn-by-melissa-bashardoust-arc-review/' rel='nofollow noopener'>HERE</a><br/><br/>This is a fantasy standalone which is one of the aspects that definitely intrigued me when I first stumbled upon this novel. I was curious to see how such a complex story could be wrapped up in a single book. I must say the author did a pretty good job and I was mostly happy with the resolutions at the end of the novel. <br/>I did think that some things were resolved way too quickly and</span>
  <span id="freeText6614387245533752477" style="display:none"><i> The ARC of this book was provided by the publisher via NetGalley in exchange for an honest review. </i><br /><br />Full review <a href="https://booksrealwhenshared.wordpress.com/2020/07/11/girl-serpent-thorn-by-melissa-bashardoust-arc-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE</a><br /><br />This is a fantasy standalone which is one of the aspects that definitely intrigued me when I first stumbled upon this novel. I was curious to see how such a complex story could be wrapped up in a single book. I must say the author did a pretty good job and I was mostly happy with the resolutions at the end of the novel. <br />I did think that some things were resolved way too quickly and also too easily. Let's just say that the thing that is supposed to be quite difficult to obtain, is actually not so hard to find. <br /><br />Soraya is a very complex character, who makes some debatable choices throughout the story. Her power is quite unique and it was definitely interesting to read about.<br /><br />In my opinion the story could have been fleshed out a little better, especially in some parts. Also, I wasn't the biggest fan of the writing, it didn't hold my attention and I didn't find it as gripping as the story would have demanded.<br /><br />If you're looking for a fantasy story with a gray main character with unique abilities, you might want to check this out!</span>

<div id="review_3225864385" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3225864385" />
    <a title="✩ Yaz ✩" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/76194326-yaz"><img alt="✩ Yaz ✩" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593729638p2/76194326.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3225864385?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✩ Yaz ✩" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✩ Yaz ✩" href="/user/show/76194326-yaz">✩ Yaz ✩</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76194326-yaz?shelf=2020-releases">2020-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76194326-yaz?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76194326-yaz?shelf=standalone">standalone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76194326-yaz?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76194326-yaz?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3225864385" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5827332127034852355">3.5 - ⭐️⭐️⭐️💫<br/><br/><i>”There was and there was not, as all stories begin, a princess cursed to be poisonous to the touch.”</i><br/><br/><b>Girl, Serpent, Thorn</b> is a reminiscent of the Persian epic known as <b>The Shahnameh</b> which enriched the book with its vivid Persian elements while also drawing inspiration from other stories particularly <b>Rappaccini’s Daughter</b>, that gave the original inspiration to the concept of a poisonous girl. <br/><br/>Let me begin by saying that this book is enjoyable, especially for readers that seek a light </span>
  <span id="freeText5827332127034852355" style="display:none">3.5 - ⭐️⭐️⭐️💫<br /><br /><i>”There was and there was not, as all stories begin, a princess cursed to be poisonous to the touch.”</i><br /><br /><b>Girl, Serpent, Thorn</b> is a reminiscent of the Persian epic known as <b>The Shahnameh</b> which enriched the book with its vivid Persian elements while also drawing inspiration from other stories particularly <b>Rappaccini’s Daughter</b>, that gave the original inspiration to the concept of a poisonous girl. <br /><br />Let me begin by saying that this book is enjoyable, especially for readers that seek a light fantasy with a character-driven plot. It’s <b>intricately detailed Persian setting</b> offers a refreshing reading experience for those that love to have a taste of other cultures in a fantastical setting.<br /><br />The elements the author draws from <b>Persian myths and legends</b> is so fascinating that it piqued my interest in wanting to explore more of Persian mythology beyond this book.<br /><br />Keeping me intrigued did not make me turn a blind eye to where this book took a less satisfying turn. <br /><br />The <b>world-building</b> I found to be really fascinating but I would’ve loved if the author fed me with more imagery because this is a world I wanted to be able to visualize in my head especially in the later parts of the book.<br /><br />The <b>plot</b> had a very solid beginning, it didn’t take long for it to progress and the twists in this are so good it fueled my excitement. If I had to divide the plot into to halves and rate them I’d say that the first half is a 4⭐️ and the second half is a 3⭐️. What primarily affected my rating were the events in the second half, I expected more action that was making its way to an epic climax, but it did not fulfill that for me.<br /><br />The <b>characters</b> that took the reins throughout this book were: <b>Soraya, Parvaneh, and Azad</b>. <br />I liked <b>Soraya</b> and what made her personality stand out to me is that she makes morally questionable actions and I got to see how internally conflicted she is. Also, she is heavily flawed; she’s easy to manipulate, reckless, selfish and indecisive and these flaws gave her more personality than the usual YA heroine.<br />The main issue I had when it came to characterization is being left underwhelmed by <b>Parvaneh</b> and <b>Azad</b> because they were the characters with a fog of mystery around them, yet when the fog lifts I was left... a little disappointed? <br /><br />The book is not heavy on <b>romance</b> but it’s definitely the subplot that was the most disappointing. None of the romances had a proper build-up to it, and we’re talking here about a stand-alone. Either choose one of the love interests and give it proper development because you do not have sequels to work on it, or do not choose one at all.<br /><br />The <b>writing</b> of the author was fluid, easy to follow and immersive. I’d say that it’s also one of the reasons this was a good read for me because the writing maintained a rhythm which made this reading experience a smooth one. <br /><br />Would I recommend this? Yes, as I stated, this still makes an enjoyable read for a light fantasy book with intriguing elements.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5827332127034852355" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review3225864385">

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('aU6OoTfophLjAA6YXIOHRexDiOzb5DqwPIDkctGlJrZA/JqoIycS7yeGnzmFh+W3zIvIAiZuNuWcPozqWcbSVA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zNrH3gWH54xdGEk7J4jLaTC01yuXbr8zmHKbbBBkQVzlaNPXEUhTcZme2Jr+jKmbEHyXxWrks2Y4zPP0mAe1vg==')})
  }
//]]>

<span id="freeTextContainer11344815988670284490">Melissa Bashardoust (pronounced BASH-ar-doost) received her degree in English from the University of California, Berkeley, where she rediscovered her love for creative writing, children’s literature, and fairy tales and their retellings. She currently lives in Southern California with a cat named Alice and more copies of Jane Eyre than she probably needs. Girls Made of Snow and Glass is her first </span>
  <span id="freeText11344815988670284490" style="display:none">Melissa Bashardoust (pronounced BASH-ar-doost) received her degree in English from the University of California, Berkeley, where she rediscovered her love for creative writing, children’s literature, and fairy tales and their retellings. She currently lives in Southern California with a cat named Alice and more copies of Jane Eyre than she probably needs. Girls Made of Snow and Glass is her first novel.<br /><br />As much as I appreciate you all, I'm not active on Goodreads, so if you'd like to get in touch, please see the contact page on my website above. Thanks and happy reading!</span>
